--- Commit Message ---
LU-15246 ptlrpc: per-device adaptive timeout parameters

When a client is mounting multiple filesystems with different
MGSes setting global parameters at_min, at_max, etc., then the
settings from one filesystem's MGS config will also apply to RPCs
sent for the OSC, MDC, and MGC devices on the other filesystem(s).
Typically the settings of the last filesystem to mount on the client
override the earlier values, and there is no way to separate them.

Moving the parameters to be per-device values allows them to be
set independently for each set of client devices, so that the
client can interact properly with each set of servers.  This allows
e.g. different timeouts for local and remote mounts, or for flash
and HDD filesystems that have different load and performance.

Add per-device adaptive timeout parameters that can optionally
replace global parameters of the same name:

    at_min     -> *.<fsname>*.at_min
    at_max     -> *.<fsname>*.at_max
    at_history -> *.<fsname>*.at_history
    ldlm_enqeue_min -> *.<fsname>*.ldlm_enqueue_min

These parameters should always be set with fsname in the device
name, rather than pure wildcard '*' device names, or it will be
be same as the global parameters in the end (settings from one
MGS will apply to devices on other filesystems).  That is a bug
in how "lctl set_param -P" works, but will be fixed separately.

Signed-off-by: Lei Feng <flei@whamcloud.com>

--- Message (Andreas Dilger, 2021-11-23 11:48:22.000000000) ---
Patch Set 3:

(3 comments)

I think this is starting to look good, but there are two things missing:
1) conf-sanity subtests to verify correct operation
2) handling two existing filesystems that are setting at_min/at_max, each for their own filesystem.
3) a deprecation warning for the global at_min/at_max that will appear in a few releases (e.g. 2.18.53).  That is enough for the new per-osc/mdc option to be available in an LTS release, so that changing over to the new parameter will not break mounting older systems.

--- Message (Andreas Dilger, 2021-11-25 01:22:08.000000000) ---
Patch Set 4:

(4 comments)

> handling two existing filesystems that are setting
 > at_min/at_max, each for their own filesystem.

I think this patch is handling only half of the problem.  It adds the per-export (MDC/OSC) at_min/at_max internal variables and tunables, which is useful, but it will not fix the original problem of a client mounting two different filesystems with different "global" at_* tunables.  It will only help in the future if only the per-export "at_*" parameters are set by the filesystem config.

This also has a secondary issue that the "at_*" parameters are supposed to be the same between the clients and servers, so setting "mdc.*.at_max" on the clients would not affect the "at_max" value that is used by the servers.  The current patch passes the per-export values back to the global value when they are zero (the default), but I think that will still have the original problem reported in .

A better solution would be to save the at_* parameters by the "config instance" number, and have unset OSC/MDC parameters use that, since the OSC/MDC device configuration can determine the cfg_instance number directly.  Then, class_process_config() would pass cfg_instance as an argument, and would need to detect when at_min/at_max parameters are in the configuration log (class_match_param(..., PARAM_SYS) and check parameter name and save them in the per-cfg_instance structure (array or rhashtable?).  That would work properly because the cfg_instance value is unique per filesystem.

In fact, some of the other parameters in lustre_attrs[] would probably also benefit from being per-filesystem (e.g. "timeout", "pinger").

--- Message (Feng Lei , 2021-11-25 02:16:58.000000000) ---
Patch Set 4:

If we want to store the at_* parameter for each cfg_instance (or equally each file system), thinking of my proposal in DDN-2407:
---------
Another proposal:

    create a sub dir under sys/fs/lustre (for example, sys/fs/lustre/fs_param)
    create sub dir for each lustre fs (sys/fs/lustre/fs_param/lustre1)
    repeat some global parameters under that dir (sys/fs/lustre/fs_param/lustre1/{at_max,at_min}

Now we can put some fs specific parameters here and overwrite global parameters.

--- Message (Andreas Dilger, 2021-11-27 01:32:10.000000000) ---
Patch Set 4:

> If we want to store the at_* parameter for each cfg_instance (or
 > equally each file system), thinking of my proposal in DDN-2407:
 > ---------
 > Another proposal:
 > 
 > create a sub dir under sys/fs/lustre (for example,
 > sys/fs/lustre/fs_param)
 > create sub dir for each lustre fs (sys/fs/lustre/fs_param/lustre1)
 > repeat some global parameters under that dir (sys/fs/lustre/fs_param/lustre1/{at_max,at_min}
 > 
 > Now we can put some fs specific parameters here and overwrite
 > global parameters.

I would rather not have a new top-level directory to hold parameters.  Normally we've stored fs-wide parameters with llite.$fsname-$instance.at_*, so that would be one option.  The other would be to store it in mgc.$nid.at_* since it will always match the scope of where different at_* values could be set (a different MGC would be created for each independent filesystem on different servers).

Patch Set 16:

This looks very nice feature. I'm wondering about eviction timeout. It seems to me this is still fully based on `obd_timeout` and won't be able to be changed, per filesystem basis, right?

--- Message (Andreas Dilger, 2021-12-22 17:49:52.000000000) ---
Patch Set 16:

(3 comments)

> This looks very nice feature. I'm wondering about eviction timeout.
 > It seems to me this is still fully based on `obd_timeout` and won't
 > be able to be changed, per filesystem basis, right?

Aurelien, I think it would be reasonable to also have timeout and ldlm_timeout on a per-filesystem (per-target) basis, but in a later patch on top of this one. The client eviction is really controlled by each target individually, there isn't really any notion of "global eviction" in Lustre.

--- Message (Aurelien Degremont, 2021-12-23 10:12:21.000000000) ---
Patch Set 16:

>The client eviction is really controlled by each target individually, there isn't really any notion of "global eviction" in Lustre.

Indeed. I really meant doing that per target, as it is done here. When available per target, this is easy to apply per filesystem tunings (mdc.*FSNAME* osc.*FSNAME* mgc.*FSNAME).

As this patch is doing this for AT parameters, it makes sense to also do the same for the static parameters that are still used even when AT is ON. That way, you can have a full per filesystem (per target) control of timeout behavior. AFAIK, this means:
 - obd_timeout
 - ldlm_timeout
 - bulk_timeout
 - ldlm_enqueue_min

?

--- Message (Andreas Dilger, 2022-08-20 22:31:07.000000000) ---
Patch Set 16: Code-Review-1

Since it isn't possible to mount targets *on the server* from different MGSes, it isn't possible for these global parameters to become inconsistent on the server, only the client.

I'm wondering if this patch would be less complex if it only addressed the client-side parameters, and stored the per-target parameters in obd_import (which is only used on the client) instead of obd_device (which is also used by the server targets)?

It looks like that was the case in v4 of this patch, but it changed in v5 of the patch.  I don't recall why that change was made, but it definitely increased the scope of this patch significantly.

It may be that my comments on v4 were not very clear.  What I was looking for is that "mdc.*.at_max", "mdc.*.timeout", etc. would be updated from the global "at_max" and "timeout" parameters when handling the config log for that filesystem/MGC, but *not* updated when handling the config log for a different MGC (different set servers).

That might be difficult to test with our test framework, because the MGS is usually shared even if there are two separate filesystems, and that makes it impossible to have two different "at_max" parameters.  The conf-sanity test would need multiple servers and a separate MGS for each one.  That can be done with autotest (usually two separate MDS nodes), but likely needs to be skipped for local developer testing.

--- Message (Andreas Dilger, 2023-01-13 23:12:29.000000000) ---
Patch Set 16:

(6 comments)

Feng, would you be able to refresh this patch again?

I think this patch is OK in the current form, despite my earlier comments.  It is definitely a large step forward, and the setting of per-OBD parameters can be done conditionally based on fsname in the future, even if it doesn't currently solve the issue of a client mounting two different filesystems with different global at_min/at_max values.  At least it would give us some way to tell the user how to fix that.

--- Message (DELBARY Gael, 2023-03-29 12:26:04.000000000) ---
Patch Set 21:

Hello guys,

Huge work, pretty interesting feature but the patch modifies too many things. Like in Lustre many services rely on adaptive timeout, the effect have to be measured...

Gael

--- Message (Andreas Dilger, 2023-03-29 20:00:35.000000000) ---
Patch Set 21:

(3 comments)

Hi Gael,
if you look at the patch, it shouldn't actually change any functionality by itself, and definitely does not affect the actual at_min, at_max, ldlm_enqueue_min values.  I thought you would be interested due to your LAD presentation on the topic.

Despite the line count, mostly what it is doing is wrapping access to the global at_min, at_max values.  ONLY IF the per-device values are changed by the admin does it have any effect.  I don't really think there is any way to make this much smaller, except splitting it into 4 separate (almost identical) patches that change at_min, at_max, at_history, and ldlm_timeout_min separately.

This patch doesn't (by itself) solve the problem of clients mounting multiple filesystems with different tunable parameters, but it starts to lay the groundwork for that.

It still needs a similar patch to make "timeout" a per-device tunable, and also a patch that makes "lctl set_param -P" settings from one MGS only apply to filesystem devices that are using that MGS, and not to all devices on the client (for at_min, at_max, timeout, but also preferably for other tunables as well).

--- Message (Andreas Dilger, 2023-04-15 02:21:02.000000000) ---
Patch Set 26:

> I must admit i'm a bit confused with all the cases where obd could
 > be NULL and we are falling back on the global values. I don't know
 > the code well enough to review, but it feels to me we will face
 > several cases, when the obd param is different than the global
 > value, where some unexpected value behavior will happen.

Aurelien, I expect that most of the places that are checking for NULL will actually have an OBD device available.  It's just hard to know this without a hundred crashes. Possibly the code could get CDEBUG() lines in the obd_get_*() functions (maybe changed to macros so they can print the source function/line) for debugging to see if any of them are actually NULL during operation. 

I _think_ there are also some cases where NULL was explicitly passed that are handled in the next patch that could be pulled forward into this patch?

 > not sure those 'extern' are useful

It definitely isn't good to declare the same function in multiple headers. I think these tiny functions could be turned into macros and add CDEBUG() to print NULL callers and we can see how much of an issue there is. That soles two issues at the same time.

--- Message (Feng Lei , 2023-04-17 06:21:44.000000000) ---
Patch Set 26:

> Patch Set 26:
> 
> > I must admit i'm a bit confused with all the cases where obd could
>  > be NULL and we are falling back on the global values. I don't know
>  > the code well enough to review, but it feels to me we will face
>  > several cases, when the obd param is different than the global
>  > value, where some unexpected value behavior will happen.
> 
> Aurelien, I expect that most of the places that are checking for NULL will actually have an OBD device available.  It's just hard to know this without a hundred crashes. Possibly the code could get CDEBUG() lines in the obd_get_*() functions (maybe changed to macros so they can print the source function/line) for debugging to see if any of them are actually NULL during operation. 
> 
> I _think_ there are also some cases where NULL was explicitly passed that are handled in the next patch that could be pulled forward into this patch?
> 
>  > not sure those 'extern' are useful
> 
> It definitely isn't good to declare the same function in multiple headers. I think these tiny functions could be turned into macros and add CDEBUG() to print NULL callers and we can see how much of an issue there is. That soles two issues at the same time.

Some facts:
1. struct obd_device is defined in obd.h
2. obd.h includes lustre_import.h through lustre_lib.h, lustre_net.h before struct obd_device is defined
3. some files include only lustre_import.h but need to call obd_get_at_xxx functions
4. if obd_get_at_xxx are declared in lustre_import.h as macros, they cannot dereference obd->obd_at_xxx members.
5. if obd_get_at_xxx are declared in obd.h after struct obd_device as macros, they cannot be accessed by files including only lustre_import.h

Unless we are willing to make some more significant changes, declaring these functions in lustre_import.h and implementing/exporting them in class_obd.c is a doable way. The declaring in obd.h can be removed.

--- Message (Andreas Dilger, 2023-04-17 09:41:37.000000000) ---
Patch Set 26:

Since declaring the macros does not actually "implement" the code, the functions are only compiled where the macros are used, so it _should_ be enough to declare them in a common location as long as struct obd is declared before they are used.

--- Message (Feng Lei , 2023-04-17 10:30:48.000000000) ---
Patch Set 26:

> Patch Set 26:
> 
> Since declaring the macros does not actually "implement" the code, the functions are only compiled where the macros are used, so it _should_ be enough to declare them in a common location as long as struct obd is declared before they are used.

When an obd_at_get_xxx() function is called, it passes an obd device pointer to the function, so it is not necessary to know the definiton of struct obd_device. But if a macro is expanded there, it needs the definition.
